# Analysis of US By County #

Updated: at 2020-09-26

For the US counties analysis, the list of all 3,143 counties (or equivalent) is sorted by the absolute number of deaths from highest to lowest.  This sorted list is then divided into two parts: counties with populations of 50,000 or more and smaller counties.

## Larger Population Counties ##

There were 990 larger population counties with a combined population of 288,662,059 (87.94% of the US population).  In these counties there have been 160,627 deaths (556.453 deaths/million) and 5,915,331 confirmed cases (20492.234 confirmed cases/million).  This group accounts for 89.21% of all US deaths and for 88.30% of all US cases.

24.42% of this group's deaths (21.78% of the total US deaths) occured in 14 counties in 10 states with a combined population of 38,155,925 (11.62% of the total US population):



The next 25.26% of this group's deaths (22.54% of the total US deaths) occured in 38 counties in 15 states with a combined population of 46,088,442 (14.04% of the total US population):



The next 25.30% of this group's deaths (22.57% of the total US deaths) occured in 112 counties in 31 states with a combined population of 71,349,668 (21.74% of the total US population)

The remaining 25.02% of this group's deaths (22.32% of the total US deaths) occured in 826 counties in 50 states with a combined population of 133,068,024 (40.54% of the total US population) 

## Smaller Population Counties ##

There were 2152 smaller population counties with a combined population of 39,577,464 (12.06% of the US population).  In these counties there have been 16,683 deaths (421.528 deaths/million) and 759,322 confirmed cases (19185.716 confirmed cases/million).  This group accounts for 9.27% of all US deaths and for 11.33% of all US cases.

24.97% of this group's deaths (2.31% of the total US deaths) occured in 77 counties in 19 states with a combined population of 2,636,648 (0.80% of the total US population):



The next 25.00% of this group's deaths (2.32% of the total US deaths) occured in 151 counties in 30 states with a combined population of 4,266,834 (1.30% of the total US population):



The next 25.00% of this group's deaths (2.32% of the total US deaths) occured in 284 counties in 35 states with a combined population of 7,015,980 (2.14% of the total US population)

The remaining 25.03% of this group's deaths (2.32% of the total US deaths) occured in 1,640 counties in 47 states with a combined population of 25,658,002 (7.82% of the total US population) 

## All US Counties ##

States and counties sorted by highest total number of deaths.  Counties with ten or fewer total deaths are not plotted nor are daily per capita rates compute for these counties.

The charts below are somewhat unusual.  The daily case and death rates per capita vary widely between US counties:  zero values occur frequently as do very large values.  We use log-log scales for these charts and add one (1) to the case and death rates before plotting.  Thus if a point is plotted at 1.0 the true value is zero, this difference is less and less visibile as rate values increase.  Adding 1.0 permits the use of log axis scales that best present these varying values.
